wrangle_act¶

I will analyze a twitter account called 'WeRateDogs'

Table of content:¶

  • Introduction
  • Gathering Data
  • Assessing Data
  • Cleaning Data
  • Storing Data
  • Visualization

Introduction¶

On this project I'll be analyzing a twitter account called 'WeRateDogs'. First we must collect three dataset for this project to succeed, the dataset are:

  • twitter-archive-enhanced.csv
  • image-predictions.tsv
  • tweet-json.txt

Gathering Data:¶

we need to import the needed library

# import library statements
import pandas as pd

In [3]:
url = 'https://d17h27t6h515a5.cloudfront.net/topher/2017/August/599fd2ad_image-predictions/image-predictions.tsv'
response = requests.get(url)
with open(url.split('/')[-1], mode='wb') as file:
    file.write(response.content)

twitter_API

In [86]:
import tweepy
from tweepy import OAuthHandler
import json
from timeit import default_timer as timer

# Query Twitter API for each tweet in the Twitter archive and save JSON in a text file
# These are hidden to comply with Twitter's API terms and conditions
consumer_key = 'HIDDEN'
consumer_secret = 'HIDDEN'
access_token = 'HIDDEN'
access_secret = 'HIDDEN'

auth = OAuthHandler(consumer_key, consumer_secret)
auth.set_access_token(access_token, access_secret)

#auth = tweepy.OAuthHandler('5Uur0mo4ol2kB8yhtZ1VxXS0u', 'h8E7fSpXWiMoBel7G1ZOAeu4Mgru0v0MtxH5ehYE1RKM89SiBH')
#auth.set_access_token('303562412-ct9aNnU0FQR0UKJVn1i1W3Y8omqSewiQWUcRaygB', 'D3qslrbdOU5fqTOp951kOIuZbkeTPBodnjNYoEGFR63Ft')


api = tweepy.API(auth, wait_on_rate_limit=True)

tweet_ids = rd.tweet_id.values
len(tweet_ids)

# Query Twitter's API for JSON data for each tweet ID in the Twitter archive
count = 0
fails_dict = {}
start = timer()
# Save each tweet's returned JSON as a new line in a .txt file
with open('tweet_json.txt', 'w') as outfile:
    # This loop will likely take 20-30 minutes to run because of Twitter's rate limit
    for tweet_id in tweet_ids:
        count += 1
        print(str(count) + ": " + str(tweet_id))
        try:
            tweet = api.get_status(tweet_id, tweet_mode='extended')
            print("Success")
            json.dump(tweet._json, outfile)
            outfile.write('\n')
        except tweepy.errors.TweepyException as e:
            print("Fail")
            fails_dict[tweet_id] = e
            pass
end = timer()
print(end - start)
print(fails_dict)

import json


data_list = []

with open('tweet-json.txt') as json_file:
    for line in json_file:
        data_list.append(json.loads(line))

store it on a DataFrame

In [8]:
json_tweet = pd.DataFrame(data_list)
In [9]:
json_data_list=[]
for i in data_list:
    tweet_id = i['id']
    retweet_count = i['retweet_count']
    favorite_count = i['favorite_count']
    json_data_list.append({'id':tweet_id , 'retweet_count': retweet_count , 'favorite_count': favorite_count})
In [10]:
j_df = pd.DataFrame(json_data_list , columns = ['id' , 'retweet_count' , 'favorite_count'])

Quality:¶

  • .csv file

      1. replace 'none' with 'NaN' on dog stages columns
      1. remove retweet and keep the original tweet 000000
      1. delete the rows in 'name' column with incorrect names
      1. change the data type 000000
      1. 'text' column must be seperated form the url

  • .json file

      1. change id to tweet_id

  • .tsv file

      1. remove unnecessry columns
      1. change the name of p1_con column to be more clear
      1. drop the 66 duplicated rows in 'jpg_url' column

Tidiness:¶

    1. compine 4 columns into one column 000000
    1. merge all the three dataframe 000000

the two plot below are for the dogs predection & dogs name:

In [80]:
# Dogs predection..


plt.figure(figsize=(10,6))
df_master['predection'].value_counts()[0:10].sort_values(ascending=True).plot(kind='barh' , color ='orange')

# declare the title of the plot and (x,y)
plt.xlabel('count',size=12)
plt.ylabel('predection', size=12)
plt.title('Dog\'s predection' , size=12)

x = df_master['predection'].value_counts()[0:10].sort_values(ascending=True).values
y= np.arange(0,10,1)

# to set the values on each bar
for x1, y1 in zip(x,y):
    plt.text(x1+1,y1,x1 , va='center')
In [81]:
# Dogs name..


plt.figure(figsize=(10,6))
df_master['name'].value_counts()[0:10].sort_values(ascending=True).plot(kind='barh' , color ='red')

# declare the title of the plot and (x,y)
plt.xlabel('count',size=12)
plt.ylabel('name', size=12)
plt.title('Dog\'s name' , size=12)

x = df_master['name'].value_counts()[0:10].sort_values(ascending=True).values
y= np.arange(0,10,1)

# to set the values on each bar
for x1, y1 in zip(x,y):
    plt.text(x1+1,y1,x1 , va='center')
